<p><sup><small>2</small></sup> Albanians are not recognized as a minority in Turkey. However approximately 500,000 people are reported to profess an Albanian identity. Of those with full or partial Albanian ancestry and others who have adopted <a href="/wiki/Turkification" title="Turkification">Turkish</a> language, culture and identity their number is estimated at 1,300,000-5,000,000 many whom do not speak Albanian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deliso38_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deliso38-6">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saunders98_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders98-9">[7]</a></sup></p>

<p><b>Albanians</b> (<a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <span lang="sq" xml:lang="sq"><i>Shqiptarët</i></span>) are an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> native to <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and neighboring countries. The term is also used to refer to the citizens of the Republic of Albania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ed_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ed-40">[38]</a></sup> Ethnic Albanians speak the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> and more than half of ethnic Albanians live in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-status-4">[a]</a></sup> A large Albanian population lives in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, with smaller Albanian populations located in Serbia and Montenegro. The majority of Albanians are nominally <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> (mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>, with a smaller <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bektashi" title="Bektashi">Bektashi</a> component), and a minority are nominally <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a>). Albanians produced many prominent figures such as <a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Skanderbeg</a>, leader of the medieval Albanian resistance to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> conquest and others during the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_National_Awakening" title="Albanian National Awakening">Albanian National Awakening</a> seeking self-determination. During the 17th and 18th century Albanians in large numbers converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, often to escape higher taxes levied on Christian subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vickers2011_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vickers2011-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Giakoumis8788_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Giakoumis8788-42">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramet203204_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramet203204-43">[41]</a></sup> As Muslims, some Albanians attained important political and military positions within the Ottoman Empire and culturally contributed to the wider Muslim world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clayer_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clayer-44">[42]</a></sup> Albania gained its independence in 1912 and between 1945-1992, Albanians lived under a repressive communist regime. Albanians within <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> underwent periods of discrimination and eventual self-determination that concluded with the breakup of that state in the early 1990s culminating with Albanians living in new countries and Kosovo. Outside the southwestern Balkans of where Albanians have traditionally been located, Albanian populations through the course of history have formed new communities contributing to the cultural, economic, social and political life of their host populations and countries while also at times assimilating too.</p>
<p>Between the 11th and 18th centuries, sizable numbers of Albanians migrated from the area of contemporary Albania to escape either various socio-political difficulties and/or the Ottoman conquest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riehl238_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Riehl238-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nasse2426_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nasse2426-46">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gogonas3_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gogonas3-47">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall2829_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hall2829-48">[46]</a></sup> One population which became the <a href="/wiki/Arvanites" title="Arvanites">Arvanites</a> settled down in southern Greece who starting from the 16th century though mainly during the 19th century onwards assimilated and today self identify as Greeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall2829_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hall2829-48">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bintliff137138_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bintliff137138-49">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liakos230_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liakos230-50">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liotta198_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liotta198-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pappas28_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pappas28-52">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VeremisKolipoulos2425_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-VeremisKolipoulos2425-53">[51]</a></sup> Another population, who became the <a href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh%C3%AB_people" title="Arbëreshë people">Arbëreshë</a> settled in southern Italy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nasse2426_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nasse2426-46">[44]</a></sup> and form the oldest continuous <a href="/wiki/Albanian_diaspora" title="Albanian diaspora">Albanian diaspora</a> producing influential and many prominent figures. Smaller populations dating to migrations during the 18th century are located on Croatia's <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatian</a> coast and scattered communities across southern Ukraine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barancic551_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barancic551-54">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Novik261262_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Novik261262-55">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Albanian diaspora also exists in a number of other countries. The largest of these is located in Turkey. It was formed during the Ottoman era through economic migration and early years of the Turkish republic through migration due to sociopolitical discrimination and violence experienced by Albanians in <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkan countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GenisMaynard553555_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-GenisMaynard553555-56">[54]</a></sup> Due to the Ottoman legacy, smaller populations of Albanians also exist in Egypt and the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, in particular Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norris209210_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norris209210-57">[55]</a></sup> In Western countries, a large and influential Albanian population exists in the United States formed from continuous emigration dating back to the 19th century. Other Albanians populations due to emigration between the 19th and 21th centuries are located in Australia, Argentina, New Zealand, Canada, Germany, Belgium, United Kingdom, France, Sweden, Switzerland, Slovenia, Croatia, Italy, Finland, Denmark, Norway, Austria, Netherlands, Bulgaria, Greece and Romania.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnonym">Ethnonym</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ethnonym">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Albanians_and_Albania" title="Names of the Albanians and Albania">Names of the Albanians and Albania</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albania_(toponym)" title="Albania (toponym)">Albania (toponym)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shqiptar" title="Shqiptar">Shqiptar</a></div>
<p>The <i>Albanians</i> (<i>Shqiptarët</i>) and their country <i>Albania</i> (<i>Shqipëria</i>) have been identified by many ethnonyms. The most common native <a href="/wiki/Ethnonym" title="Ethnonym">ethnonym</a> is <i>Shqiptar</i>, pl. <i>Shqiptarë</i>; the name "Albanians" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greek" title="Byzantine Greek">Byzantine Greek</a>: <i>Albanoi/Arbanitai/Arbanites</i>; <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>: <i>Albanenses/Arbanenses</i>) was used in medieval Greek and Latin documents that gradually entered European languages from which other similar derivative names emerged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsie200534_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie200534-58">[56]</a></sup> From these <a href="/wiki/Ethnonym" title="Ethnonym">ethnonyms</a>, names for Albanians were also derived in other languages that were or still are in use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BardhylDemiraj534_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-BardhylDemiraj534-60">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamusella241_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusella241-61">[59]</a></sup> In English <i>Albanians</i>; Italian <i>Albanesi</i>; German <i>Albaner</i>; Greek <i>Arvanites</i>, <i>Alvanitis</i> (Αλβανίτης) plural: <i>Alvanites</i> (Αλβανίτες), <i>Alvanos</i> (Αλβανός) plural: <i>Alvanoi</i> (Αλβανοί); Turkish <i>Arnaut</i>, <i>Arnavut</i>; <a href="/wiki/South_Slavic_languages" title="South Slavic languages">South Slavic languages</a> <i>Arbanasi</i>, <i>Albanci</i> (Албанци); <a href="/wiki/Aromanian_language" title="Aromanian language">Aromanian</a> <i>Arbineş</i> and so on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liotta198_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Liotta198-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BardhylDemiraj534_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-BardhylDemiraj534-60">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamusella241_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusella241-61">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murati71_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Murati71-62">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koukoudis34_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Koukoudis34-63">[61]</a></sup> The term for a people located in the area of contemporary Albania is first encountered in the works of Byzantine historian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Attaliates" title="Michael Attaliates">Michael Attaliates</a>. He referred to them as <i>Albanoi</i> having taken part in a revolt against the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in 1043 and to the <i>Arbanitai</i> as subjects of the duke of Dyrrachium (modern <a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durrës">Durrës</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadgearuGordon25b_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-MadgearuGordon25b-64">[62]</a></sup> These references have been disputed as to whether they refer to Albanians in an ethnic sense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadgearuGordon25b_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-MadgearuGordon25b-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pritsak5253_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pritsak5253-65">[63]</a></sup> A later reference to Albanians from the same Attaliates regarding the participation of Albanians in a rebellion around 1078 is undisputed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadgearuGordon25_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-MadgearuGordon25-66">[64]</a></sup> In later Byzantine usage, the terms "Arbanitai" and "Albanoi" with a range of variants were used interchangeably, while sometimes the same groups were also called by the classicising name Illyrians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finlay37_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Finlay37-69">[67]</a></sup> The first reference to the Albanian language dates to the latter 13th century (around 1285).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ethnonym <i>Albanian</i> has been hypothesized to be connected to and stem from the <i><a href="/wiki/Albanoi" title="Albanoi">Albanoi</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vasiliev613_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vasiliev613-71">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jelavich25_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jelavich25-72">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShabanDemiraj481_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShabanDemiraj481-73">[71]</a></sup> an Illyrian tribe mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> with their centre at the city of <a href="/wiki/Albanopolis" title="Albanopolis">Albanopolis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M.C3.ABnikuCampos2_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-M.C3.ABnikuCampos2-74">[72]</a></sup> Linguists believe that the <i>alb</i> part in the root word originates from an Indo-European term for a type of mountainous topography, of which other words such as <i><a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">alps</a></i> is derived from.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malcolm29_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malcolm29-75">[73]</a></sup> Through the root word <i>alban</i> and its rhotacized equivalents <i>arban</i>, <i>albar</i>, and <i>arbar</i>, the term in Albanian became rendered as <i>Arbëneshë/Arbëreshë</i> for the people and <i>Arbënia/Arbëria</i> for the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsie200534_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie200534-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup> The Albanian language was referred to as <i>Arbnisht</i> and <i>Arbërisht</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M.C3.ABnikuCampos2_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-M.C3.ABnikuCampos2-74">[72]</a></sup> While the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exonym" title="Exonym">exonym</a> Albania for the general region inhabited by the Albanians does have connotations to Classical Antiquity, the Albanian language employs a different ethnonym, with modern Albanians referring to themselves as <i>Shqip(ë)tarë</i> and to their country as <i>Shqipëria</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup> Two etymologies have been proposed for this ethnonym: one, derived from the etymology from the Albanian word for eagle (shqipe, var.,shqiponjë).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamusella241_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusella241-61">[59]</a></sup> In Albanian <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a>, this word denotes a bird <a href="/wiki/Totem" title="Totem">totem</a>, dating from the times of Skanderbeg as displayed on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanian_flag" title="Albanian flag">Albanian flag</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamusella241_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusella241-61">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ej2-s_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-ej2-s-76">[74]</a></sup> The other is within scholarship that connects it to the verb 'to speak' (<i>me shqiptue</i>) from the Latin "<i>excipere</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamusella241_61-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusella241-61">[59]</a></sup> In this instance the Albanian endonym like <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slav_(ethnonym)" title="Slav (ethnonym)">Slav</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym#Tendencies_in_the_development_of_exonyms" title="Endonym">and others</a> would originally have been a term connoting "those who speak [intelligibly, the same language]".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamusella241_61-5"><a href="#cite_note-Kamusella241-61">[59]</a></sup> The new ethnonyms <i>Shqip(ë)tarë</i> and <i>Shqipëria</i> emerged and replaced the older ethnonyms <i>Arbëneshë/Arbëreshë</i> and <i>Arbënia/Arbëria</i> between the late 17th and early 18th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup> That era brought about religious and other sociopolitical changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-6"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup> As such a new and generalised response by Albanians based on ethnic and linguistic consciousness to this new and different Ottoman world emerging around them was a change in ethnonym.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloshi277_59-7"><a href="#cite_note-Lloshi277-59">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Illyria" title="Illyria">Illyria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Albanians" title="Origin of the Albanians">Origin of the Albanians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Arb%C3%ABr" title="Principality of Arbër">Principality of Arbër</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Albania_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Albania (medieval)">Kingdom of Albania (medieval)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanian_Principalities" title="Albanian Principalities">Albanian Principalities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamization_of_Albania" title="Islamization of Albania">Islamization of Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Albania" title="History of Albania">History of Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kosovo" title="History of Kosovo">History of Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_tribes_of_Albania" title="List of tribes of Albania">List of tribes of Albania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Albania" title="List of wars involving Albania">List of wars involving Albania</a></div>
<p>Studies in genetic anthropology show that the Albanians share the same ancestry as most other European peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Belledi480486_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Belledi480486-77">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albanians_in_the_Middle_Ages">Albanians in the Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Albanians in the Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>What is possibly the earliest written reference to the Albanians is that to be found in an old Bulgarian text compiled around the beginning of the 11th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsie3_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie3-78">[76]</a></sup> It was discovered in a Serbian manuscript dated 1628 and was first published in 1934 by Radoslav Grujic. This fragment of a legend from the time of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsar_Samuel" title="Tsar Samuel">Tsar Samuel</a> endeavours, in a catechismal 'question and answer' form, to explain the origins of peoples and languages. It divides the world into seventy-two languages and three religious categories: Orthodox, half-believers (i.e. non-Orthodox Christians) and non-believers. The Albanians find their place among the nations of half-believers. If the dating of Grujic is accepted, which is based primarily upon the contents of the text as a whole, this would be the earliest written document referring to the Albanians as a people or language group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsie3_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie3-78">[76]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>It can be seen that there are various languages on earth. Of them, there are five Orthodox languages: Bulgarian, Greek, Syrian, Iberian (Georgian) and Russian. Three of these have Orthodox alphabets: Greek, Bulgarian and Iberian. There are twelve languages of half-believers: Alamanians, <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, Magyars (Hungarians), Indians, Jacobites, Armenians, <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, Lechs (Poles), <b>Arbanasi</b> (Albanians), Croatians, Hizi, Germans.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:129px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karl_Topia,_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku,_Ardenica_Monastery.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="403" data-file-width="247" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Karl_Topia%2C_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku%2C_Ardenica_Monastery.png/127px-Karl_Topia%2C_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku%2C_Ardenica_Monastery.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Karl_Topia%2C_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku%2C_Ardenica_Monastery.png/190px-Karl_Topia%2C_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku%2C_Ardenica_Monastery.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Karl_Topia%2C_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku%2C_Ardenica_Monastery.png 2x" width="127"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karl_Topia,_by_Kostandin_Shpataraku,_Ardenica_Monastery.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Karl_Topia" title="Karl Topia">Karl Topia</a> powerful feudal prince and warlord in late 14th century Albania</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first undisputed mention of Albanians in the historical record is attested in Byzantine source for the first time in 1079–1080, in a work titled <i>History</i> by Byzantine historian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Attaliates" title="Michael Attaliates">Michael Attaliates</a>, who referred to the <i>Albanoi</i> as having taken part in a revolt against <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> in 1043 and to the <i>Arbanitai</i> as subjects of the duke of <a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durrës">Dyrrachium</a>. It is disputed, however, whether the "Albanoi" of the events of 1043 refers to Albanians in an ethnic sense or whether "Albanoi" is a reference to <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Normans</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> under an archaic name (there was also a tribe in Italy by the name of "Albanoi").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadgearuGordon25b_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-MadgearuGordon25b-64">[62]</a></sup> However a later reference to Albanians from the same Attaleiates, regarding the participation of Albanians in a rebellion around 1078, is undisputed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadgearuGordon25_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-MadgearuGordon25-66">[64]</a></sup> At this point, they are already fully Christianized, although <a href="/wiki/Albanian_mythology" title="Albanian mythology">Albanian mythology</a> and folklore are part of the <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Balkan_mythology" title="Paleo-Balkan mythology">Paleo-Balkan</a> pagan mythology,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bonnefoy253_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bonnefoy253-79">[77]</a></sup> in particular showing Greek influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EliadeAdams179_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-EliadeAdams179-80">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the late 11th century the Albanians were called Arbën/Arbër and their country as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arbanon" title="Arbanon">Arbanon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norris35_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norris35-81">[79]</a></sup> a mountainous area to the west of Lake Ochrida and the upper valley of the river Shkumbin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicol160_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nicol160-82">[80]</a></sup> It was in 1190, when the rulers of Arbanon (local Albanian noble called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progon_of_Kruja" title="Progon of Kruja">Progon</a> and his sons Dhimitër and Gjin) created their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Arb%C3%ABr" title="Principality of Arbër">principality</a> with its capital at <a href="/wiki/Kruj%C3%AB" title="Krujë">Krujë</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ducellier780a_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ducellier780a-83">[81]</a></sup> After the fall of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Progon" title="House of Progon">Progon Dynasty</a> in 1216, the principality came under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grigor_Kamona" title="Grigor Kamona">Grigor Kamona</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulam_of_Albania" title="Gulam of Albania">Gulam of Albania</a>. Finally the Principality was dissolved in 1255. Around 1230 the two main centers of Albanian settlements, one around <a href="/wiki/Devoll_(river)" title="Devoll (river)">Devoll river</a> in what is now central Albania,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ducellier780781_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ducellier780781-84">[82]</a></sup> and the other around the region which was known with the name Arbanon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ducellier780781b_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ducellier780781b-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:166px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="394" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg/164px-Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg/246px-Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg/328px-Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg.png 2x" width="164"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coa_Kastrioti_Family.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kastrioti_family" title="Kastrioti family">Kastrioti family</a> Coat of Arms</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1271 <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Naples" title="Charles I of Naples">Charles of Anjou</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Albania_(medieval)" title="Kingdom of Albania (medieval)">Kingdom of Albania</a>, after he captured a part of the <a href="/wiki/Despotate_of_Epirus" title="Despotate of Epirus">Despotate of Epirus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> A major attempt to advance further in direction of Constantinople failed at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Berat_(1280%E2%80%931281)" title="Siege of Berat (1280–1281)">Siege of Berat (1280–1281)</a>. A Byzantine counteroffensive soon ensued, which drove the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_House_of_Anjou" title="Capetian House of Anjou">Angevins</a> out of the interior by 1281. The <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_Vespers" title="Sicilian Vespers">Sicilian Vespers</a> further weakened the position of Charles, and the Kingdom was soon reduced by the <a href="/wiki/Epirus_(region)" title="Epirus (region)">Epirotes</a> to a small area around <a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durrës">Durrës</a>. The kingdom however held out until 1368, when the city was captured by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Topia" title="Karl Topia">Karl Thopia</a>. The presence of the kingdom reinforced the influence of Catholicism and the conversion to its rite, not only in the region of Durrës but in other parts of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> A new wave of Catholic dioceses, churches and monasteries were founded, a number of different religious orders began spreading into the country, and papal missionaries also reached the territories of the Kingdom of Albania. Those who were not Catholic in Central and North Albania converted and a great number of Albanian clerics and monks were present in the Dalmatian Catholic institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 14th century a number of <a href="/wiki/Albanian_principalities" title="Albanian principalities">Albanian principalities</a> were created. These included <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Kastrioti" title="Principality of Kastrioti">Principality of Kastrioti</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Dukagjini" title="Principality of Dukagjini">Principality of Dukagjini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Albania_(medieval)" title="Principality of Albania (medieval)">Princedom of Albania</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Gjirokast%C3%ABr" title="Principality of Gjirokastër">Principality of Gjirokastër</a>. At the beginning of the 15th century these principalities became stronger, especially because of the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>. Some of these principalities were united in 1444 under the military alliance called <a href="/wiki/League_of_Lezh%C3%AB" title="League of Lezhë">League of Lezha</a>.</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" style="text-align:center">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albanians_under_the_Ottoman_Empire">Albanians under the Ottoman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Albanians under the Ottoman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:150px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="349" data-file-width="285" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg/148px-Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg/222px-Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg 2x" width="148"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gjergj_Kastrioti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Gjergj Kastrioti Skanderbeg</a> — renowned military leader of the 25 year Albanian rebellion against the Ottomans</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:153px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mehmedpasha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="370" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mehmedpasha.jpg/151px-Mehmedpasha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mehmedpasha.jpg/226px-Mehmedpasha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Mehmedpasha.jpg/302px-Mehmedpasha.jpg 2x" width="151"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mehmedpasha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Köprülü Mehmed Pasha was the most powerful <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" title="Grand Vizier">Ottoman grand vizier</a> of Albanian origin and founder of the Köprülü dynasty.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the dawn of the establishment of the Ottoman Empire in Southeast Europe, the geopolitical landscape was marked by scattered kingdoms of small principalities. The Ottomans erected their garrisons throughout southern Albania by 1415 and established formal jurisdiction over most of Albania by 1431.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> However, in 1443 a great and longstanding revolt broke under the lead of the Albanian national hero Skanderbeg, which lasted until 1479, many times defeating major Ottoman armies led by sultans <a href="/wiki/Murad_II" title="Murad II">Murad II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed II</a>. Skanderbeg united initially the Albanian princes and later established a centralized authority over most of the non-conquered territories, becoming Lord of Albania. He also tried relentlessly but rather unsuccessfully to create a European coalition against the Ottomans. He frustrated every attempt by the Turks to regain Albania, which they envisioned as a springboard for the invasion of Italy and western Europe. His unequal fight against the mightiest power of the time won the esteem of Europe as well as some support in the form of money and military aid from Naples, the papacy, <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Ragusa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-91">[89]</a></sup> Finally after decades of resistance, Ottomans captured <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Shkodra" title="Siege of Shkodra">Shkodër in 1479</a> and Durrës in 1501.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> Skanderbeg's long struggle to keep Albania free became highly significant to the Albanian people, as it strengthened their solidarity, made them more conscious of their national identity, and served later as a great source of inspiration in their struggle for national unity, freedom, and independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-91">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-initaly_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-initaly-93">[91]</a></sup> The invasion triggered a several waves of migration of Albanians from Albania, Epirus and <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnese</a> to the south of Italy, constituting an <a href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh%C3%AB_people" title="Arbëreshë people">Arbereshe</a> community. Albanians were recruited all over Europe as a light cavalry known as <a href="/wiki/Stratioti" title="Stratioti">stratioti</a>. The stratioti were pioneers of light cavalry tactics during this era. In the early 16th century heavy cavalry in the European armies was principally remodeled after Albanian stradioti of the Venetian army, Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Hussar" title="Hussar">hussars</a> and German mercenary cavalry units (Schwarzreitern).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the 16th century, Ottoman rule over Southeast Europe was largely secure. The Ottomans proceeded in stages, first appointing a <a href="/wiki/Qadi" title="Qadi">qadi</a> along with governors and then military retainers in the cities. <a href="/wiki/Timar" title="Timar">Timar</a> holders, not necessarily converts to Islam, would occasionally rebel, the most famous case of which is <a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Skanderbeg</a>. His figure would be used later in the 19th century as a central component of Albanian national identity. Ottoman control over the Albanian territories was secured in 1571 when <a href="/wiki/Ulcinj" title="Ulcinj">Ulcinj</a>, presently in <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, was captured.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:183px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="347" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg/181px-Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg/272px-Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg 2x" width="181"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dupr%C3%A9_-_Ali_Pasha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ali_Pasha_of_Tepelena" title="Ali Pasha of Tepelena">Ali Pasha of Tepelena</a> was one of the most powerful Muslim Albanian rulers of the late 18th and early 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="644" data-file-width="659" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg/220px-16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg/330px-16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg/440px-16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:16th_century_Albanian_costumes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Albanian men in the 16th Century - <i>Codice de trajes</i> 1547</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most significant impact on the Albanians was the gradual <a href="/wiki/Islamization" title="Islamization">Islamization</a> process of a large majority of the population, although such a process only became widespread in the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clayer_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clayer-44">[42]</a></sup> Mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholics" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> converted in the 17th century, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Orthodox</a> Albanians became <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> mainly in the following century. Initially confined to the main city centres of <a href="/wiki/Elbasan" title="Elbasan">Elbasan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shkod%C3%ABr" title="Shkodër">Shkodër</a>, by this time the countryside was also embracing the new religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clayer_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-Clayer-44">[42]</a></sup> In Elbasan Muslims made up just over half the population in 1569–70 whereas in Shkodër this was almost 90% and in <a href="/wiki/Berat" title="Berat">Berat</a> closer to 60%. In the 17th century, however, Catholic conversion to Islam increased, even in the countryside. The motives for conversion according to scholars were diverse, depending on the context. The lack of source-material does not help when investigating such issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clayer_44-3"><a href="#cite_note-Clayer-44">[42]</a></sup> Areas such as Albania, Western Macedonia, Southern Serbia, Kosovo, parts of northern Greece and southern Montenegro in Ottoman sources were referred to as <i>Arnavudluk</i> (آرناوودلق) or Albania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anscombe200688_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anscombe200688-95">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anscombe772_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anscombe772-96">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolovos41_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kolovos41-97">[95]</a></sup> The Ottoman period that followed in Albania after the end of Skanderbeg's resistance was characterized by other changes. Many Albanians gained prominent positions in the Ottoman government such as: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iljaz_Hoxha" title="Iljaz Hoxha">Iljaz Hoxha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamza_Kastrioti" title="Hamza Kastrioti">Hamza Kastrioti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koca_Davud_Pasha" title="Koca Davud Pasha">Koca Davud Pasha</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Za%C4%9Fanos_Pasha" title="Zağanos Pasha">Zağanos Pasha</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC_Mehmed_Pasha" title="Köprülü Mehmed Pasha">Köprülü Mehmed Pasha</a> (head of the Köprülü family of Grand Viziers), the <a href="/wiki/Bushati_family" title="Bushati family">Bushati family</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulejman_Pasha" title="Sulejman Pasha">Sulejman Pasha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edhem_Pasha" title="Edhem Pasha">Edhem Pasha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nezim_Frakulla" title="Nezim Frakulla">Nezim Frakulla</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haxhi_Shekreti" title="Haxhi Shekreti">Haxhi Shekreti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Zyko_Kamberi" title="Hasan Zyko Kamberi">Hasan Zyko Kamberi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ali_Pasha_of_Gucia" title="Ali Pasha of Gucia">Ali Pasha of Gucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">Muhammad Ali of Egypt</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ali_Pasha_of_Tepelena" title="Ali Pasha of Tepelena">Ali Pasha of Tepelena</a> who rose to become one of the most powerful Muslim Albanian rulers in western <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a>. During the Ottoman era Albanians involved in imperial service could also be found across the empire in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and across the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> as vital military and administrative retainers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norris196_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norris196-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albanian_national_awakening">Albanian national awakening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Albanian national awakening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanian_national_awakening" title="Albanian national awakening">Albanian national awakening</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:140px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume,_cca_1913.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4983" data-file-width="2420" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume%2C_cca_1913.tif/lossy-page1-138px-Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume%2C_cca_1913.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume%2C_cca_1913.tif/lossy-page1-208px-Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume%2C_cca_1913.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume%2C_cca_1913.tif/lossy-page1-277px-Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume%2C_cca_1913.tif.jpg 2x" width="138"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nopcsa_Ferenc_in_shqiptar_warrior_costume,_cca_1913.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Albanian warrior costume in 1913</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_(Jun-Nov_1912).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="789" data-file-width="1183" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_%28Jun-Nov_1912%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_%28Jun-Nov_1912%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_%28Jun-Nov_1912%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_%28Jun-Nov_1912%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_%28Jun-Nov_1912%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_%28Jun-Nov_1912%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Albanian_Provisional_Government_(Jun-Nov_1912).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag used during the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_National_Awakening" title="Albanian National Awakening">Albanian National Awakening</a> and by early 20th century Albanian rebels<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsie_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elsie-99">[97]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the 1870s, the <a href="/wiki/Sublime_Porte" title="Sublime Porte">Sublime Porte</a>'s reforms aimed at checking the Ottoman Empire's disintegration had clearly failed. The image of the "Turkish yoke" had become fixed in the nationalist mythologies and psyches of the empire's Balkan peoples, and their march toward independence quickened. Because of the higher degree of Islamic influence, the Albanians internal social divisions, and the fear that they would lose their Albanian-populated lands to the emerging Balkan states—<a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>—were the last of the Balkan peoples to desire division from the Ottoman Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Birth_of_Albania_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Birth_of_Albania-100">[98]</a></sup> The Albanian national awakening as a coherent political movement began after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Stefano" title="Treaty of San Stefano">Treaty of San Stefano</a>, according to which Albanian-inhabited areas were to be ceded to other states of the Balkans, and focused on preventing that partition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaser_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaser-101">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Brien_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Brien-102">[100]</a></sup> The Treaty of San Stefano was the impetus for the nation-building movement, which was based more on fear of partition than national identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Brien_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Brien-102">[100]</a></sup> Even after Albania became independent in 1912, Albanian national identity was fragmented and possible non-existent in much of the new country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Brien_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Brien-102">[100]</a></sup> The state of disunity and fragmentation would remain until the communist period following World War II, when the communist nation-building project would achieve greater success in nation-building and reach more people than any previous regime, thus creating Albanian national communist identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Brien_102-3"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Brien-102">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1167" data-file-width="1237" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png/220px-AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png/330px-AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png/440px-AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AlbaniansOutsideAlbania.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Distribution of Albanians in neighboring countries.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Europe">Southeast Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Southeast Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Approximately 7 million Albanians are to be found within the Balkan peninsula with about half this number residing in Albania and the other divided between <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and to a much smaller extent <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>. An estimated 2.2 million Albanians live in the territory of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_Yugoslavia" title="Former Yugoslavia">Former Yugoslavia</a>, the greater part (close to two million) in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-status_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-status-4">[a]</a></sup> Rights to use the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian language</a> in education and government were given and guaranteed by the 1974 Constitution of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SFRY" title="SFRY">SFRY</a> and were widely utilized in Macedonia and in Montenegro before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Yugoslavia" title="Dissolution of Yugoslavia">Dissolution of Yugoslavia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Albania">Albania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Albania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Albania" title="Demographics of Albania">Demographics of Albania</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> has an estimated 3 million inhabitants, with ethnic Albanians comprising approximately 95% of the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kosovo">Kosovo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kosovo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Kosovo" title="Albanians in Kosovo">Albanians in Kosovo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:153px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albania-ethnique1898.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="568" data-file-width="342" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Albania-ethnique1898.jpg/151px-Albania-ethnique1898.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Albania-ethnique1898.jpg/227px-Albania-ethnique1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Albania-ethnique1898.jpg/302px-Albania-ethnique1898.jpg 2x" width="151"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albania-ethnique1898.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ethnographic map of Balkans (detail), <i>Atlas Général Vidal-Lablache</i>, Paris, 1898.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Albanian presence in Kosovo and in the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Toplica_District" title="Toplica District">Toplica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moravac" title="Moravac">Morava</a> regions is recorded since the medieval period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anscombe767774785788_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anscombe767774785788-105">[103]</a></sup> As the Serbs expelled a large number of Albanians from the wider Toplica and Morava regions in southern Serbia, which the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> of 1878 had given to the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade Principality</a>, a large number of them settled in Kosovo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jagodic_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jagodic-106">[104]</a></sup> In Kosovo they and their descendants are known as <i>muhaxher</i> (meaning <i>the exiled</i>, from the Arabic muhajir).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uka525354_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Uka525354-107">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a> of 1912-13, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Montenegro</a> - after expelling the Ottoman forces in present-day Albania and Kosovo - committed numerous war crimes against the Albanian population, which were reported by the European, American and Serbian opposition press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo war</a>, Serbian paramilitary forces committed war crimes in Kosovo, although the Serbian government claims that the army was only going after suspected Albanian terrorists. This triggered a <a href="/wiki/NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" title="NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">78-day NATO campaign</a> in 1999. Now Albanians in Kosovo constitute the majority with 1,616,869.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> The most widespread religion among Albanians in Kosovo is <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a>; the other religion Kosovar Albanians practice is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Kosovo" title="Roman Catholicism in Kosovo">Roman Catholicism</a>). Culturally, Albanians in Kosovo are very closely related to Albanians in Albania. Traditions and customs differ even from town to town in Kosovo itself. The spoken dialect is <a href="/wiki/Gheg_Albanian" title="Gheg Albanian">Gheg</a>, typical of northern Albanians. The language of state institutions, education, books, media and newspapers is the standard dialect of Albanian, which is closer to the <a href="/wiki/Tosk_Albanian" title="Tosk Albanian">Tosk</a> dialect.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Republic of Macedonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Albanians in the Republic of Macedonia">Albanians in the Republic of Macedonia</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Serbia" title="Albanians in Serbia">Albanians in Serbia</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Montenegro">Montenegro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Montenegro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Montenegro" title="Albanians in Montenegro">Albanians in Montenegro</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Greece" title="Albanians in Greece">Albanians in Greece</a></div>
<p>An estimated 275,000–600,000 Albanians live in Greece, forming the largest immigrant community in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> They are economic migrants whose migration began in 1991, following the collapse of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_People%27s_Republic_of_Albania" title="Socialist People's Republic of Albania">Socialist People's Republic of Albania</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arvanites" title="Arvanites">Arvanites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albanian-speakers_of_Western_Thrace" title="Albanian-speakers of Western Thrace">Albanian-speakers of Western Thrace</a> are a group descended from <a href="/wiki/Tosks" title="Tosks">Tosks</a> who migrated to southern and central Greece between the 13th and 16th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gogonas3_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gogonas3-47">[45]</a></sup> They are Greek Orthodox Christians, and though they traditionally speak a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Tosk_Albanian" title="Tosk Albanian">Tosk Albanian</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Arvanitika" title="Arvanitika">Arvanitika</a>, they have fully assimilated into the Greek nation and do not identify as Albanians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall2829_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hall2829-48">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bintliff137138_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bintliff137138-49">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VeremisKolipoulos2425_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-VeremisKolipoulos2425-53">[51]</a></sup> Arvanitika is in a state of attrition due to language shift towards Greek and large-scale internal migration to the cities and subsequent intermingling of the population during the 20th century.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cham_Albanians" title="Cham Albanians">Cham Albanians</a> were a group that formerly inhabited a region of <a href="/wiki/Epirus_(region)" title="Epirus (region)">Epirus</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Chameria" title="Chameria">Chameria</a>, nowadays <a href="/wiki/Thesprotia" title="Thesprotia">Thesprotia</a> in northwestern Greece. Most Cham Albanians converted to Islam during the Ottoman era. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> Chams were <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Cham_Albanians" title="Expulsion of Cham Albanians">expelled</a> from Greece during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, by an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EDES" title="EDES">anti-communist resistance group</a>, as a result of their participation in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EAM-ELAS" title="EAM-ELAS">communist resistance group</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis-Cham_Albanian_collaboration" title="Axis-Cham Albanian collaboration">collaboration</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_occupation_of_Greece_during_World_War_II" title="Axis occupation of Greece during World War II">Axis occupation</a>, while Orthodox Chams have largely assimilated into the Greek nation.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Albanian_diaspora" title="Albanian diaspora">Albanian diaspora</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

<td class="mbox-image">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh%C3%AB_people" title="Arbëreshë people">Arbëreshë people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arbanasi_people" title="Arbanasi people">Arbanasi people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Ukraine" title="Albanians in Ukraine">Albanians in Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_of_Romania" title="Albanians of Romania">Albanians of Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Italy" title="Albanians in Italy">Albanians in Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_of_Croatia" title="Albanians of Croatia">Albanians of Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Germany" title="Albanians in Germany">Albanians in Germany</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Switzerland" title="Albanians in Switzerland">Albanians in Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Sweden" title="Albanians in Sweden">Albanians in Sweden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Albanians in the United Kingdom">Albanians in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:239px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albanians_in_Europe.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1266" data-file-width="2230" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Albanians_in_Europe.jpg/237px-Albanians_in_Europe.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Albanians_in_Europe.jpg/356px-Albanians_in_Europe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Albanians_in_Europe.jpg/474px-Albanians_in_Europe.jpg 2x" width="237"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albanians_in_Europe.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Albanians in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Italy has a historical Albanian minority of 260,000 which are scattered across <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">Southern Italy</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh%C3%AB_people" title="Arbëreshë people">Arbëreshë</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nasse2426_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-Nasse2426-46">[44]</a></sup> They had settled in Italy between the 15th and 16th century, displaced by the changes brought about by the expansion of the Ottoman Empire in the Balkans. The Arbëreshë were offered refuge by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Kingdom of Naples</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a> (both under <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Aragonese</a> rule) and given their own villages and protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> The Arbëreshë speak <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh_language" title="Arbëresh language">Arbërisht</a></i>, an old variant of Albanian spoken in southern Albania, known as <a href="/wiki/Tosk_Albanian" title="Tosk Albanian">Tosk Albanian</a>. The Arbëreshë are scattered throughout southern Italy and Sicily, and in small numbers also in other parts of Italy. They are in great numbers in North and Latin America, especially in the USA, Brazil, Argentina, Chile, Uruguay and Canada. The Arbëreshë constitute one of the largest minorities in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> The majority of Albanians in Italy arrived in 1991 and have since surpassed the older populations of Arbëreshë. After the breakdown of the communist regime in Albania in 1990, Italy had been the main immigration target for Albanians leaving their country. This was because Italy had been a symbol of the West for many Albanians during the communist period, because of its geographic proximity.</p>
<p>There are small Albanian populations dating to migrations from the 18th century. One group known as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arbanas" title="Arbanas">Arbanas</a></i> are located on Croatia's Dalmatian coast and fled Ottoman repression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barancic551_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barancic551-54">[52]</a></sup> The second known as the <i>Албанці</i> (Albantsi) are located in scattered communities across southern Ukraine and descend from Albanian warriors who fought against the Ottoman Empire during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Russo-Turkish_wars" title="History of the Russo-Turkish wars">Russo-Turkish wars</a> and allowed to settle in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Novik261262_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Novik261262-55">[53]</a></sup> The actual number of the Albanian population in Romania is unofficially estimated at around 10,000 persons. Most members of the community live in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>,<sup>[2]</sup> while the rest mainly live in larger urban centers such as <a href="/wiki/Timi%C8%99oara" title="Timișoara">Timișoara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ia%C8%99i" title="Iași">Iași</a>, Constanțaand <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>. Most families in Romania are Orthodox and trace their origins to the area around <a href="/wiki/Kor%C3%A7%C3%AB" title="Korçë">Korçë</a>.</p>
<p>Approximately 1 million are dispersed throughout the rest of Europe. These are mainly refugees from Kosovo that migrated during the Kosovo war. During the Kosovo war in 1999, many Kosovo Albanians sought asylum in the Federal Republic of Germany. By the end of 1999, the number of Kosovo Albanians in Germany was about 480,000, about 100,000 had returned voluntarily after the war in their homeland or been forcibly removed. The cities with the largest population of Germans of Albanian descent are the metropolitan regions of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>. In Berlin in 1999, there were about 25,000 Albanians; the number dropped because of remigration and Germany's general population decline. In Sweden, Albanians number approximately 54,000. As of 2011 there are approximately 100,000 Albanians living in the United Kingdom.</p>
